text:
This was a MESS!  I consulted with someone I know that works in an Itailan restaurant, and this is NOT the way you make them!  All you need is a few beaten eggs, and some itailan flavored bread crumbs with a little garlic powder mixed in. First dip the mozz. sticks in the egg mixture then the italian bread crumbs, then back in the egg mixture then back in the bread crumb mixture. Make sure they are completely coated. The oil shouldn't be any hotter then 350 degrees, then put the sticks in the oil for just about a minute, just until they float up to the top of the surface, and they're done! You can also use the same procedure with a block of mozz. Just don't cut the block any thicker then 1/4 inch. I hope this helps.

text:
These were delicious and not hard to make. My minor improvisations included: cutting the cheese sticks in half (so my 8 became 16) and using plain bread crumbs with about 2 tsps mixed Italian seasoning. I also followed the advice of several reviewers: First, I combined the flour/starch mixture with the breadcrumbs. It was a huge time-saver and didn't seem to impact the end result. I also tried both double & triple coating and found that a double coat was sufficient for my taste. When the batter got a little clumpy, I simply moulded the clumps around the cheese for a slightly thicker coat. This part was a little messy, but other than that, it wasn't too bad. I coated all of the sticks before frying and set them aside on a plate. This turned out to be great advice because the frying really only takes about 30 seconds, and if you turn your back for too long, the sticks will burn. I did not have any problem with cheese leaking out, and the end result was truly restaurant quality. I will definitely make this recipe again!

text:
Ok, I was a sceptic if this could be done at home! THANK YOU! I am a Happy Believer!!! I just finished making a batch of these and I am still smiling...WOW! This was SUPER! First to make it easy and to make sure they "looked" like cheese sticks-shape-wise, I used Sargento Mozarella sticks, I unwrapped each and cut in half. I had 3 separate bowls setup w/ mixtures as described. I dipped each moz stick in egg mix, then flour mix, then egg mix, then bread crumb mix-making sure they were coated well. Then I put in oil. NOT ONE leaked!! I had to watch these little suckers cause they brown really fast! I let them cool a few minutes and served with little cups of pizza sauce for dipping. My 4 kids and hubby ADORED them and can't get enough. Considering these cost alot on dinners out--they are a KEEPER! WORD OF ADVICE: Use latex gloves to keep hands clean, this can get messy, and if making more than a dozen the mixes get goopy, so for large batches have extra mixes ready! otherwise..would give 10 stars if I could! THANKS SO MUCH!

text:
This recipe is great on its own so I will give 5 stars. But the techniques used are all wrong. Here is what I do: Cut the cheese sticks in half this makes them easier to work with. Mix the flour with the bread crumbs and nix the cornstarch, dip the cheese in plain flour first to help the egg stick, then dip in crumbs, eggs again, then again in breadcrumbs/flour mix you will have a nice thick coating on them. Place them on a baking sheet covered in wax paper as you assemble them, then when you finish place the the tray in the freezer for about 30 minutes! (This is KEY! This keeps the cheese from melting the second it hits the oil and allows the coating to get crisp first) The recipe is pretty good as is, but if you make them as stated they will turn out a big mess!

OK, I tried them as stated and they work without fail. Working in the food industry I have come across many different versions of this recipe. This is how the big name restaurants make theirs honestly! Freezing the cheese works well about the time it is cooked on the outside it is warmed through. Also the method is flour first, then egg, then crumbs. and get creative! For gods sake use any type of cheese that make you happy, and as far as crumbs use any type of (stale) bread you like and toss it in the processor! Add spices you like, and serve it with any sauce you think will work. It is food not plutonium! It don't bite and you get to eat the mistakes! How much better can it get?

text:
I used this recipe New Year's day for a yummy snack for the family!  Our 10 yr old is a mozza stick afficianado and he proclaimed them to be the BEST! He asked me to make more the next day!  I didn't have brick mozzarella on hand, but instead had shredded mozzarella. I preformed the mozza into about 30 balls. I then coated all the balls (about 4 at a time) in the flour mixture in a medium sized mixing bowl. In the same manner I then coated them in the egg mixture, using a fork,then directly into another medium sized bowl into PANKO bread crumbs, then placed them on a platter. (in the meantime I was preheating my frying oil) These steps save on mess! The key is to fry only about 5 or 6 at a time, because as soon as they begin to brown slightly, you turn them and then quickly remove them to a plate. The cheese really doesn't take long to melt! If you leave them in too long that's when you end up with a gooey mess!

text:
I didn't freeze the cheese beforehand, but having it chilled in the fridge worked fine. I mixed in my garlic powder, Italian seasoning, a little salt and some black pepper in the Italian bread crumbs.  I double battered my chilled cheese and then put in my deep fryer at 350 degrees for about 45 seconds or so. Also, I cooked about 4 at a time to keep them from sticking to each other. When I first attempt to remove a cheese stick from the basket, it started to fall a bit limp, so before i gathered the others, I just let it sit for a few minutes before transferring them to our serving dish. Doing this allowed the cheese to cool just right and let it keep its form when handling, yet still be melty in the middle. I may try freezing cheese for about 30 minutes before i cook them next time to see what happens. Also, next time i will combine all dry ingredients to save a step. overall, nice and easy recipe and will definitely make this again.

Very yummy!!! So much better than the ones you buy in the freezer Isle at the grocery store. My family loved them. Although messy I found it necessary to dip them in egg then flour re-dip in the egg and coat with breadcrumbs. I tried them without the flour and the cheese ran out. I used Italian seasoned  Panko bread crumbs because I like the outside crispy and they were perfect. I found that 1/2 to 1 hour in the freezer or refrigerator was enough, the longer the cheese was in the cold the longer it took for it to melt when fried, and it didn't take long for them to brown in the hot oil. Thank you for this awesome recipe!

NON MESSY ALERT!!  Keep your hands as dry as possible, have a towel nearby.  Put the bread crumbs, garlic, flour, corn starch in a large tupperware bowl that you have the lid for.  After dipping in the eggs, take about 4 at a time to the tupperware bowl, put on the lid and shake lightly.  With dry hands, find them and put them onto a plate.  Do this at least 3 TIMES PER STICK

i combined the bread crumbs, garlic, flour and cornstarch together in a tupperware bowl.   Just used eggs in the other bowl.  Had the mozz stix frozen.  I ended up dipping them 3 times in each.  Had the deep fryer set to 350 and cooked for about 2 minutes and 15 seconds.  turned out amazing!!!  one of the best recipes on here!

I just tried this recipe and the mozzarella sticks are great! I made it according to the directions, but I did add two steps. After dipping the cheese into the flour,egg and bread crumbs,the coating didn't seem thick enough to hold the melted cheese; so I added two steps. After the first coating I let them dry for 10 minutes and then coated them a second time and let them dry for another 10 minutes. They are perfect and I know that my guests will love them tonight!

text:
For all fried mozzarella cheese lovers.  This receipe is an excellent recipe for the fried cheese goodness we treat ourselves to from time to time.   I noticed quite a few of the pics that the cheese is globbing  out of a lot of the time.   The 2 huge things I change from this receipe is as follows:  Cut  your sticks from one large chunk of mozzarella chesse.  I use whole-milk mozzi cheese found in a 1 lb. brick in every grocery store in America.  It is 2 inches thick and in approximately 5 x 5 inch square.  Cut the Mozzi cheese into 1/2 inch slices. ( a little thicker cut will not make a difference)  You should end up with a 1/2 inch thick and 5 inch long and 2 inches wide pieces.  Bread cheese slices as directed in this recipe.  MOST important!  Put the breaded cheese sticks in the freezer for 1 hour.  When your oil is heated to proper temperature just drop them in and watch them get beautiful brown and crispy (approx. 1 - 2 minutes)   WITHOUT the cheese gobbing out of the sticks.  I promise they are hot and gooey all the way through. YUMMO!

text:
In order to get better adhesion, I soaked the fresh cut mozzarella sticks in water for a couple minutes before covering with the flour mixture. This helps ensure the egg mixture sticks properly. Then the sticks are individually placed in the egg mixture with one hand and rubbed down to ensure full coverage. This hand places them into the bread crumb mixture and the other hand coats them with crumbs preventing the crumbs and eggs from mixing which causes clumping and waste. 

Instead of Italian Seasoning, you can also try mixing your bread crumbs with Herbes de Provence for a slight twist.

Well, after a few personal mistakes, these ended up turning out very well! Just a little tip to others who may be short a few brain cells as I seem to be: Be sure to leave a good 2 inches of oil from the top of the pan! B/c if it spills over, it WILL cause a stove fire! But I'm sure most ppl will know that. Now, with that aside, after my outrageous mistake, the next night I tried making these again, and they turned out wonderful! I have a huge weakness for mozzarella sticks! So it was probably very dangerous for me to find this recipe! (In more ways than one!) :-) But they were very good, and not messy to make! text:
This recipe is soooooo good! I combined the flour/cornstarch mixture and the breadcrumb mixture and it did not affect the final product. I used Polly-O part skim mozzarella string cheese (9 sticks) and cut them in half to make 18 mozzarella sticks. I dipped them into the egg wash, then the breadcrumbs, the egg wash, and then the breadcrumbs again. Then I froze them for 20 minutes. Instead of deep-frying them, I put a few tablespoons of olive oil into a pan and pan-fried them. None of the cheese oozed out and the ending result was DEFINITELY restaurant-quality. Thanks!

text:
These turned out so good- I'm amazed at how easy they really are to make. First of all, I completely forgot to add the cornstarch, so you actually don't even need it, and mine turned out great.  Second, these are very, very messy to make, but half way through I figured out an easy way to do it.  I used a toothpick to pierce each cheese stick, and used it to dip the stick in the egg mixture, bread crumbs, back to egg mixture, then again to the crumb mixture. After dipping, I just removed the toothpick and moved on to the next one.  Try it that way from the beginning and it will save you a lot of mess.  After coating all of the cheese sticks, I let them rest for about 15 minutes so the breading had a chance to adhere.  I served with my own recipe for marinara sauce- they were a huge hit with my family. I will never buy storebought cheese sticks again!  Thanks for sharing the recipe!

city:

region:
None
country:
None
text:
Like any recipe that requires battering, the prep for these mozzarella sticks was pretty messy, but the end result is amazing. After reading some reviews I made a few changes: 

- I dipped once in flour, and twice in the egg and breadcrumb mixture. This gave the breadcrumb crust a nice texture and thickness and may have prevented the cheese from oozing out of gaps in the coating, but if you're planning on freezing the battered cheese sticks before frying I think only one coat is necessary.
- I froze my cheese sticks for about an hour before frying. This stopped the cheese from oozing in the fryer, but after 30 seconds of frying, the cheese was still cold in the center. I would recommend frying a bit longer or microwaving before serving in order to get that stringy effect when you pull the cheese sticks apart.

None
text:
This recipe did not work for me because the coating does not adequately seal and protect the mozzarella sticks from melting and escaping into the frying oil.  For starters, the eggs are excessively thinned and lose their ability to effectively hold the bread crumbs. Only a teaspoon or so of water should be added to the beaten eggs.  Even with less thinned eggs it is still necessary to coat the cheese sticks three or four times; once with flour and two or three times with bread crumbs (egg wash between each dry coating). Oil can be as hot as 375F.  The shorter time the cheese sticks are in the oil the less chance there is of the coating breaking and the cheese melting into the oil or oil into cheese stick. The need for cornstarch in the flour is questionable. Do not use toasted bread crumbs or panko.  Adding a teaspoon of onion powder improved the flavor of the breading.

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
I modified this recipe after trying making it the way listed above. It didn't have the flavor I was looking for so I started playing with it and came up with this and my family LOVED them. I mixed 3 eggs in a bowl, poured Italian flavored bread crumbs on a plate mixed with garlic powder not garlic salt, I'm not a huge salt person, then on another plate I put flour on it. I cut up the mozzarella to desired size, dipped it in the egg mixture, then the bread crumb mixture, back in the egg mixture, then into the flour, back into the egg mixture, and finally back into the bred crumb mixture. Seems like a lot, but it gave it great flavor and a good breading on it (we liked it with a little bit of a thicker breading) 

side note: I used my hands and had to wash them after making a few mozzarella sticks because the mixture would stick to my hands, so if you don't like getting your hands dirty I don't suggest this for you. =)

city:

text:
These were so amazingly awesome that I could have sworn I was eating at a restaurant that serves these! If you want to avoid the mess of the mozzarella leaking out while frying, the solution is so simple it almost hurts . . . make sure it's coated evenly and well with the egg so that the bread crumbs have the whole surface to stick to. Sure, you may still get some melty cheese leaking here or there, but really, you're frying cheese, and if you expect that not to be messy then you've really never cooked before. I've made these 3 or 4 times now, and my fiancee and mom are always begging for more. They even microwave pretty well for mozzarella sticks (it helps them stay crispy if they're on a paper towel in the micro, just be careful that they don't start leaking, because they don't take long at all to reheat! 20-30 seconds or so). Oh, and add seasoned salt, garlic salt, and pepper to the breadcrumbs if you want a little extra oomph (or are lacking in dipping sauces! LOL My mistake the 2nd time around), otherwise a good bbq, ranch, or marinara goes great with these, with or without the added spices.

text:
I give this 5 stars for taste and texture and about 4 1/2 stars for technique. The only thing that I changed in this was dipping it in egg first then flour and bread crumbs. By the time the cheese stick gets to the bread crumbs it didnt want to stick so i dipped it in egg then flour then egg again and then finally bread crumbs and it coated it well and came out perfectly crispy and melty. If you like gooey cheese sticks then let them cool for a few minutes before eating. I deep fried them for about 1 minute instead of 30 seconds because i wanted a good color to them. Great recipe!

text:
Great basic recipe, but more seasoning is always a plus, in my book!  I also had a hard time at the end of the batch because my dry mix got too wet, and I actually had to "pat" it on-- and the sticks with all that thick batter weren't as tasty as the ones from the beginning of the batch.  Next time, I'll split my dry ingredients into two or three bowls so when one portion gets too moist, I can just move on to the next fresh (dry!) portion and get consistent results all the way through.  (But, really, you just can't go wrong with breaded, fried CHEESE at any rate!)

text:
This was a pretty good recipe.  I tried one batch using the information as is, and the mozzarella sticks did not hold their shape too well as there was leaking.  The second batch I double coated and they came out so much better.  I didn't have garlic salt, so I used 1/2 garlic powder and 1/2 salt, although I think I will just use garlic powder next time because they didn't need the salt in my opinion.  I also didn't have a mess, I picked up the sticks and dipped them in all the ingredients carefully using tongs and none of the coating was removed...easier to take care of my 4 month old when I don't have to constantly wash my hands!  All in all, good recipe, fun to make and the best part...a great way to use up leftover mozzarella!

city:
None
region:
None
country:
None
text:
These are delicious!  I tried a few reviewers' suggestions: I put the cheese (string chesse cut in half) in the freezer for a few minutes while I mixed the other stuff and heated the oil.  I mixed all the dry stuff together, using parmesan bread crumbs, 1 tsp. garlic powder, 1/2 tsp. salt, and about 2 tbsp. italian seasonings.  I did the dry/wet hand method suggested by another reviewer.  There was plenty of dry stuff that I could push over the wet cheese so that my dry hand stayed dry.  I did double dip for two layers of breading.  I put all the breaded cheeses on a cookie sheet when they were done and then fried them in a deep fryer, 8 at a time.  I counted to about 40 and then pulled them out.  The breading had wonderful flavor!  I will probably use less flour/cornstarch next time as I had a lot of dry mix left at the end.  A few of them oozed a little and some were still a bit firm in the middle, so I'm not sure if I'd do the freezing thing first again.  I don't mind a little oozing and I'd rather have them all melty inside.  We dipped them in some leftover sauce from the World's Best Lasagna recipe here on AllRecipes.  I'll definitely be making these again as everyone in my family loves them!

These were pretty good. I used a 1 lb block of mozzarella cheese and cut them into little rectangles. I did have to batter the cheese twice, which meant I had to double the egg and flour mixture. I froze the cheese for 20 mins before frying them and a few still leaked. I did make more than what we could eat in one sitting, so I froze the rest. When I cooked them, they didn't leak so maybe that's the secret. I wanted to mention that using the block cheese made the sticks very stringy just like the restaurants (I read some reviewers complain that their sticks did not pull strings when eaten). Anyhow, I don't think it was worth the mess/ trouble because they tasted just like the frozen kind.

These are so easy to make.  I dipped in egg, flour, egg, and then bread crumbs per other reviews.  Make sure you don't forget to cover the ends with the mixtures otherwise the cheese will escape from there.  I heated oil in the skillet on the stove. Thanks for the great recipe!

These were a little messy when dipping and coating, but they were tastey.  I used block mozzarella and sliced into 1/4" thick x 3/4" wide x 2-1/2" long pieces.  Instead of Italian bread crumbs, I used a blender and chopped white toast into a fairly fine consistency.  I added about 1/4 teaspoon of Italian seasoning to the bread crumbs.  Don't deep fry too long or the coating will get too dark and the cheese will start to ooz.  We dipped these in pizza sauce from a jar.

DEFINITELY freeze stick before hand. We rushed the first batch and they melted into a puddle and sunk to the bottom. Don't just season the bread crumbs, season the flour and eggs too. After 3 steps of breading, do another layer of egg and crumbs to get a better seal and thicker crust (and therefore more flavor).

These were really yummy, but I quickly found out I couldn't follow the recipe exactly. First, I used egg whites (that's all I had.) Second, I ended up having to double coat the cheese sticks. The first couple I made ended up breaking and oozing all over. My kids loved them--even my daughter who isn't a fan of cheese sticks usually.

text:
Combine the cornstarch, garlic salt, 1 c. seasoned breadcrumbs, and 1/2 c. plain panic in a bowl.  Plain flour in another bowl. 2 beaten eggs in another bowl.  Dip the half-sticks in flour, then egg, then crumb mixture and put on foil-lined cookie sheet. Keep going. Now some of the wet egg is showing thru the coating. SOTHEN go back and roll them one more time in the bread-crumb-panko mixture. Onto the foil pan and into the freezer for at least 30 minutes.  PERFECT every time ;-)

text:
You definitely have to double dip these.  Coat in either flour or cornstarch (but it's not necessary for both), then egg, crumbs, egg, and crumbs again.  I make these in large batches and freeze them after breading, that way I can store them in a baggie in the freezer and cook as many or as few as I want at the time.  Oil no hotter than 350, and when you see the first bit of cheese seeping out of the crust on any sticks, they're done.

None
text:
Cut the cheese sticks in half this makes them easier to work with. Mix the flour with the bread crumbs and nix the cornstarch, dip the cheese in plain flour first to help the egg stick, then dip in crumbs, eggs again, then again in breadcrumbs/flour mix you will have a nice thick coating on them. Place them on a baking sheet covered in wax paper as you assemble them, then when you finish place the the tray in the freezer for about 30 minutes! This keeps the cheese from melting the second it hits the oil and allows the coating to get crisp first

For those that dont like the starch egg crumbs combo, the starch is there to keep the breadcrumbs from adhering to the cheese directly. Makes them way easier to reheat later as well as provide a flavor barrier. Its a great way to do it and I'm glad to see it.

I made a few batches of these. One was as per the recipe (except I used a block of mozzarella cut into sticks). This turned out great as well but did allow for more cheese to melt out of the sticks (still not a lot).

text:
Very easy if you set everything up prior to start.   I used a cooking thermometer and a cast iron frying pan.  Cut the mozzarella sticks in half and put them in the freezer.  I did not have Italian b.c's.  Just added seasonings to the regular b.c.'s I had to taste.  I did the double dip, using the one wet/one dry method and used a fork to turn and move sticks.  The prepared sticks were placed on a cookie sheet and then put 6-8 in the oil for 30-40 seconds.  Placed on cake rake with paper towel.  This is basically what most reviewers said and they turned out wonderful with rave reviews.

As other reviewers have mentioned, I combined the starches into a single bowl. To prepare the sticks for frying, I double-dipped them to coat them sufficiently (egg, then starches, then egg, then starches). These turned out wonderfully and are a favorite of the family.

One thing that I noted is that these are great when eaten with marinara sauce but when eaten plain are a little bland. If you like them plain, I definitely recommend spicing up the batter a bit. Excellent recipie!

text:
CHECK THIS OUT..:::..I find that this recipe works better if you use slightly frozen/refrigerated cheese sticks. Also, dip the the cheese stick twice in the bread crumbs; so, after the 1st dip in the bread crumbs>>> dip the c.sticks in the egg mix>>> then dip in the bread crumbs. Also the bread mix taste better with more Italian season and garlic salt (but don't overdo it). Again, freezing the c.sticks before coating or after coating helps too! Keep a close eye on sticks is a must; I walked away from the sticks for almost a min, when i came back the cheese was seeping into the oil. However, they still were okay.

country:
None
text:
I didn't use cornstarch, so I can't say I made the recipe exactly, but this was so delicious!  My boyfriend (who considers himself a mozz. stick connoiseur) absolutely loved these.  I used Sargento Light String cheese cut in half, and these worked perfectly!  However, I've made this twice with string cheese and both times it lacked that stringy, melted quality that makes mozzarella sticks fun.  Next time, I will chop mozzarella from a block for this recipe.

I double-coated in this order: flour, egg, crumbs, egg, crumbs. Make sure to dust off extra all extra flour before sticking it into the egg mixture, then letting excess egg drip off before putting it into the bread crumb mixture.  This coats those suckers more easily and its less messy overall.  I had absolutely no leaking when the sticks went in the oil.  (But keep an eye on them, because these things brown super fast!)

If you're a fan of garlic flavor, I would go ahead and double the amount of garlic salt in the recipe.  My roommate preferred it when i made that adjustment to suit her own tastes.

text:
This was pretty good. Kind of messy, but they turned out ok. To get the coating to stay on I dipped the cheese sticks into egg, then the breading, then the flour, back into the egg and then the breading again. It stayed on fine. Cheese did bubble out into the oil, but they stayed together.
It seems that the breading on the cheese stix in restaraunts is thicker or something.
These passed the craving test though so I'm not complaining.
Thanks Nanci.
